         </a>
        </th>

         </code>
        </td>

         </div>

          <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">

         </b>
         Without proper
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          rendering support
         </a>
         , you may see
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">
          question marks, boxes, or other symbols
         </a>
         instead of
         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          Help:IPA
         </a>

        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Romanian
       </b>
       (obsolete spellings
       <b>
        Rumanian
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Roumanian
       </b>
       ; autonym:
       <i>
        limba română
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Romanian" title="Help:IPA/Romanian">
         [ˈlimba roˈmɨnə]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small class="nowrap">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ro-Limba_Rom%C3%A2n%C4%83.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/Ro-Limba_Rom%C3%A2n%C4%83.ogg" title="Ro-Limba Română.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       , "the Romanian language", or
       <i>
        românește
       </i>
       , lit. "in Romanian") is an
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Romance_languages" title="Eastern Romance languages">
        East Romance language
       </a>
       spoken by approximately 24–26 million people
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as a native language, primarily in
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">
        Moldova
       </a>
       , and by another 4 million people as a second language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28mil_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-28mil-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has official status in Romania and the Republic of Moldova. It is one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_European_Union" title="Languages of the European Union">
        official languages of the European Union
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Romanian is a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Romance_languages" title="Eastern Romance languages">
        Balkan-Romance
       </a>
       group that evolved from several dialects of
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       separated from the
       <a href="/wiki/Italo-Western_languages" title="Italo-Western languages">
        Western Romance
       </a>
       during the 5th–8th centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       To distinguish it within that group in comparative linguistics it is called
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daco-Romanian" title="Daco-Romanian">
         Daco-Romanian
        </a>
       </i>
       as opposed to its closest relatives,
       <a href="/wiki/Aromanians" title="Aromanians">
        Aromanian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Megleno-Romanian_language" title="Megleno-Romanian language">
        Megleno-Romanian
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Istro-Romanians" title="Istro-Romanians">
        Istro-Romanian
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       During
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moldovan_SSR" title="Moldovan SSR">
        Soviet times
       </a>
       —and to some extent even today—Romanian was called
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">
         Moldovan
        </a>
       </i>
       in the Republic of Moldova, although the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Moldova" title="Constitutional Court of Moldova">
        Constitutional Court
       </a>
       ruled in 2013 that "the official language of the republic is Romanian".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moldova_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Moldova-9">
         [nb 1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Immigrant Romanian speakers are scattered across many other countries, notably Australia, Italy, Spain, Ukraine, Bulgaria, the United States, Canada, Brazil, Mexico, Argentina, Greece, Turkey, Russia, Portugal, the United Kingdom, Cyprus, Israel, France and Germany.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Romanian" title="History of Romanian">
        History of Romanian
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistory">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Romance_languages" title="Eastern Romance languages">
        Eastern Romance languages
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Romanian_language" title="Proto-Romanian language">
        Proto-Romanian language
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Romance_substratum" title="Eastern Romance substratum">
        Eastern Romance substratum
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_superstratum_in_Romanian" title="Slavic superstratum in Romanian">
        Slavic superstratum in Romanian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Romanian_words_of_possible_Dacian_origin" title="List of Romanian words of possible Dacian origin">
        List of Romanian words of possible Dacian origin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_the_Romanians" title="Origin of the Romanians">
        Origin of the Romanians
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Romance_languages" title="Eastern Romance languages">
        Eastern Romance languages
       </a>
       , like the other branches of
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       , descend from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       , adopted in
       <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">
        Dacia
       </a>
       by a process of
       <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">
        Romanization
       </a>
       during early centuries AD.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The influence of the military in Dacia is due to the distribution of the military units in this bridgehead of the Roman Empire's defense (two legiones, 12 alae, 41 cohortes and 13 numeri), contrary, e.g., to that of the Rhenish army, which was concentrated at the
       <a href="/wiki/Limes_Germanicus" title="Limes Germanicus">
        Germanic limes
       </a>
       and so left little influence on the local spoken Gallo-Latin. The identification of numerous words of military (Dacian-)Roman usage – 52 semantic specific changes and inherited military Latin words with their classical meanings – is at the heart of the hypothesis that the Romanian language is the continuation of the military Latin spoken in the north-eastern frontier region of the Roman Empire. These vestiges of military usage are unique to Romanian in its language family.
      </p>
      <p>
       Thus, Romanian is scientifically very interesting from a linguistic and historical viewpoint, since Romance languages did not prevail in the other frontier regions of the Roman Empire in Europe, Asia and Africa, although Africa's falling under Arab sway surely played a role in the ultimate demise of any Romance dialect. Also, the conservation in Romanian of these numerous vestiges of Latin military slang (sermo castrensis) – such as
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          a (se)aține
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to waylay"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          coif
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("helmet"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          împărat
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("emperor"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          a împresura
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to encircle with pressure"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          a (se) (în)cumeta
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to venture"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          a înțina
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to make thin a tree for its collapse on the invaders"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          aținat
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("made thin a tree"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          mire
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "fiancé" (&lt; Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <i>
          miles
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "soldier", metonymy),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          a purcede
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to advance"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          a răpune
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to kill"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          rost
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "sense" a.s.o. (&lt; Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <i>
          rostrum
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "beak at prow of Roman warship"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          (f)sat
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "village" (&lt; Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <i>
          fossatum
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "trench for defence",
       <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">
        metonymy
       </a>
       ),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          șes
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "plain" (&lt; Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <i>
          sessus
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "plain place for camping", metonymy),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          a supune
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ("to subject"),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          tindă
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "veranda" (&lt; Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <i>
          tenda sub vallo
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "tent out of agglomerated fortress", metonymy),
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <i>
          țară
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "homeland" (&lt; Lat.
       <i>
        <span lang="la">
         <i>
          terra
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       "earth" ˃ Arom.
       <i>
        țară
       </i>
       "earth"), etc. and their absence in Aromanian (Balkan Romanian dialect spoken in peaceful area) – indicates the continuity of the
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Latinophone" title="wikt:Latinophone">
        Latinophones
       </a>
       in the northern Danubian region, this despite dire and constant defensive wars with
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">
        Germanic
       </a>
       , "
       <a href="/wiki/Turan" title="Turan">
        Turanian
       </a>
       "
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness">
          <span title="This information is too vague. (April 2017)">
           vague
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">
        Turkic peoples
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magyars" title="Magyars">
        Magyars
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">
        Slavic
       </a>
       populations who entered and eventually settled there.
      </p>
      <p>
       This linguistic evidence challenges the Roeslerian theory. The vestiges from Latin military slang particularize the Romanian language in the neolatin area, together with its isolated history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to Cristian Mihail, the Roslerian theory is annihilated because of the fact that the Romanian words in common with the Albanian words not preserve the sound „l” between vowels – in accordance, i.e. with Rom. "māgurā" and Alb. "magulë" etc. – likewise with Romanian words from Latin linguistic stratum (Rom. "scara" &lt; Lat. "scala" etc.) unlike the words from Slavic later stratum, which preserve the sound „l” intervowels (cf. Rom. "mila", no "*mira" &lt; Sl. "mila") would prove that the Romanian words in common with the Albanian words proceed of a latter stratum in Balkan region, near the Albanians, as supporting also by linguistics the continuity of the Latinophons (Romanians) in the Nordic-Danubian region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       withdrew from
       <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">
        Dacia
       </a>
       in 271–272 AD, leaving it to the
       <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">
        Goths
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The history of Eastern Romance between the 3rd century and the development of
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Romanian_language" title="Proto-Romanian language">
        Proto-Romanian
       </a>
       by the 10th century, when the area came under the influence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       , is unknown. It is
       <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_the_Romanians" title="Origin of the Romanians">
        a matter of debate
       </a>
       whether
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Romanian" title="Proto-Romanian">
        Proto-Romanian
       </a>
       developed among
       <a href="/wiki/Daco-Roman" title="Daco-Roman">
        Romanized people
       </a>
       who were left behind in Dacia by the Roman withdrawal or among Latin-speakers in the Balkans south of the Danube.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the High and
       <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">
        Late Middle Ages
       </a>
       , Romanian became influenced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">
        Slavic languages
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and to some degree by Greek. Romanian remains unattested throughout the Middle Ages, and only enters the historical record in the early 16th century.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">
        Early history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Cleanup" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This article may
          <b>
           require
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">
            cleanup
           </a>
          </b>
          to meet Wikipedia's
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">
           quality standards
          </a>
          . The specific problem is:
          <b>
           This section presents modern Romanian translations as if they were historical sources.
          </b>
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           if you can.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (January 2018)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The use of the denomination
       <i>
        Romanian
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        română
       </i>
       ) for
       <i>
        our beautiful language
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        limba noastră cea frumoasă
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) and use of the demonym
       <i>
        Romanians
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Români
       </i>
       ) for speakers of this language predates the foundation of the modern Romanian state. Although the followers of the former Romanian voievodships used to designate themselves as "Ardeleni" (or "Ungureni"), "Moldoveni" or "Munteni", the name of "rumână" or "rumâniască" for the Romanian language itself is attested earlier, during the 16th century, by various foreign travellers into the Carpathian Romance-speaking space,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as in other historical documents written in Romanian at that time such as
       <a class="extiw" href="https://ro.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letopise%C8%9Bul_%C8%9A%C4%83rii_Moldovei" title="ro:Letopisețul Țării Moldovei">
        Cronicile Țării Moldovei
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        The Chronicles of the land of Moldova
       </i>
       ) by
       <a href="/wiki/Grigore_Ureche" title="Grigore Ureche">
        Grigore Ureche
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1534,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tranquillo_Andronico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tranquillo Andronico (page does not exist)">
        Tranquillo Andronico
       </a>
       notes:
       <i>
        "Valachi nunc se Romanos vocant"
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        The Wallachians are now calling themselves Romans
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Francesco della Valle writes in 1532 that Romanians
       <i>
        are calling themselves Romans in their own language
       </i>
       , and he subsequently quotes the expression:
       <i>
        "Știi Românește?"
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Do you know Romanian?
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After travelling through
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Wallachia" title="Principality of Wallachia">
        Wallachia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Moldavia" title="Principality of Moldavia">
        Moldavia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Transylvania_(1570%E2%80%931711)" title="Principality of Transylvania (1570–1711)">
        Transylvania
       </a>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ferrante_Capecci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ferrante Capecci (page does not exist)">
        Ferrante Capecci
       </a>
       accounts in 1575 that the indigenous population of these regions call themselves "românești" (
       <i>
        "romanesci"
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Lescalopier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Lescalopier (page does not exist)">
        Pierre Lescalopier
       </a>
       writes in 1574 that those who live in Moldavia, Wallachia and the vast part of Transylvania,
       <i>
        "se consideră adevărați urmași ai romanilor și-și numesc limba "românește", adică romana"
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        they consider themselves as the descendants of the Romans and they name their language Romanian
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transylvanian_Saxon" title="Transylvanian Saxon">
        Transylvanian Saxon
       </a>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Johann_Lebel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Johann Lebel (page does not exist)">
        Johann Lebel
       </a>
       writes in 1542 that
       <i>
        "Vlachi" se numeau între ei "Romuini"
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_people" title="Polish people">
        Polish
       </a>
       chronicler
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stanislaw_Orzechowski" title="Stanislaw Orzechowski">
        Stanislaw Orzechowski
       </a>
       (Orichovius) notes in 1554 that
       <i>
        în limba lor "walachii" se numesc "romini"
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        In their language the Wallachians call themselves Romini
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Croatian_people" title="Croatian people">
        Croatian
       </a>
       prelate and diplomat
       <a href="/wiki/Antun_Vran%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Antun Vrančić">
        Antun Vrančić
       </a>
       recorded in 1570 that
       <i>
        "Vlachs in Transylvania, Moldavia and Wallachia designate themselves as "Romans"
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">
        Transylvanian Hungarian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Szentiv%C3%A1nyi" title="Martin Szentiványi">
        Martin Szentiványi
       </a>
       in 1699 quotes the following:
       <i>
        «Si noi sentem Rumeni»
       </i>
       ("Și noi suntem români" – "We are Romans as well") and
       <i>
        «Noi sentem di sange Rumena»
       </i>
       ("Noi suntem de sânge român" –
       <i>
        We are of Roman blood
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a class="extiw" href="https://ro.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palia_de_la_Or%C4%83%C8%99tie" title="ro:Palia de la Orăștie">
        Palia de la Orăștie
       </a>
       (1582) stands written
       <i>
        «.[...] că văzum cum toate limbile au și înfluresc întru cuvintele slăvite a lui Dumnezeu numai noi
        <b>
         românii
        </b>
        pre limbă nu avem. Pentru aceia cu mare muncă scoasem de limba jidovească si grecească si srâbească pre limba
        <b>
         românească
        </b>
        5 cărți ale lui Moisi prorocul si patru cărți și le dăruim voo frați
        <b>
         rumâni
        </b>
        și le-au scris în cheltuială multă... și le-au dăruit voo fraților
        <b>
         români
        </b>
        ,... și le-au scris voo fraților
        <b>
         români
        </b>
        "
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in Letopisețul Țării Moldovei written by the Moldavian chronicler Grigore Ureche we can read:
       <i>
        «În Țara Ardialului nu lăcuiesc numai unguri, ce și sași peste seamă de mulți și
        <b>
         români
        </b>
        peste tot locul...»
       </i>
       ("In Transylvania there live not solely Hungarians or Saxons, but overwhelmingly many Romanians everywhere around.").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nevertheless, the oldest extant document written in Romanian remains
       <a href="/wiki/Neac%C8%99u%27s_letter" title="Neacșu's letter">
        Neacșu's letter
       </a>
       (1521) and was written using Cyrillic letters (which remained in use up until the late 19th century). There are no records of any other documents written in Romanian from before 1521.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Miron_Costin" title="Miron Costin">
        Miron Costin
       </a>
       , in his
       <i>
        De neamul moldovenilor
       </i>
       (1687), while noting that Moldavians,
       <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">
        Wallachians
       </a>
       , and the Romanians living in the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       have the same origin, says that although people of Moldavia call themselves
       <i>
        Moldavians
       </i>
       , they name their language
       <i>
        Romanian
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        românește
       </i>
       ) instead of
       <i>
        Moldavian
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        moldovenește
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ConstantiniuSincer_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ConstantiniuSincer-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Dimitrie_Cantemir" title="Dimitrie Cantemir">
        Dimitrie Cantemir
       </a>
       , in his
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/la:Descriptio_Moldaviae" title="s:la:Descriptio Moldaviae">
         Descriptio Moldaviae
        </a>
       </i>
       (Berlin, 1714), points out that the inhabitants of Moldavia, Wallachia and Transylvania spoke the same language. He notes, however, some differences in accent and vocabulary.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cantemir's work provides one of the earliest histories of the language, in which he notes, like
       <a href="/wiki/Grigore_Ureche" title="Grigore Ureche">
        Ureche
       </a>
       before him, the evolution from Latin and notices the Greek and Polish borrowings. Additionally, he introduces the idea that some words must have had
       <a href="/wiki/Dacian_language" title="Dacian language">
        Dacian
       </a>
       roots. Cantemir also notes that while the idea of a Latin origin of the language was prevalent in his time, other scholars considered it to have derived from Italian.
      </p>
      <p>
       The slow process of Romanian establishing itself as an official language, used in the public sphere, in literature and ecclesiastically, began in the late 15th century and ended in the early decades of the 18th century, by which time Romanian had begun to be regularly used by the Church. The oldest Romanian texts of a literary nature are religious manuscripts (
       <i>
        Codicele Voroneţean
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Psaltirea Scheiană
       </i>
       ), translations of essential Christian texts. These are considered either propagandistic results of confessional rivalries, for instance between
       <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">
        Lutheranism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">
        Calvinism
       </a>
       , or as initiatives by Romanian monks stationed at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C4%83p%C3%A2n%C5%A3a" title="Săpânţa">
        Peri Monastery
       </a>
       in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maramure%C5%9F" title="Maramureş">
        Maramureş
       </a>
       to distance themselves from the influence of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mukacheve" title="Mukacheve">
        Mukacheve
       </a>
       eparchy in Ukraine.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The language remains poorly attested during the Early Modern period.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">
        Modern history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/National_awakening_of_Romania" title="National awakening of Romania">
        National awakening of Romania
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first
       <a href="/wiki/Romanian_grammar" title="Romanian grammar">
        Romanian grammar
       </a>
       was published in Vienna in 1780.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elementa_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Elementa-32">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following the
       <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia#Annexation_by_the_Russian_Empire" title="Bessarabia">
        annexation of Bessarabia by Russia
       </a>
       (after 1812), Moldavian was established as an official language in the governmental institutions of
       <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">
        Bessarabia
       </a>
       , used along with Russian,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The publishing works established by Archbishop
       <a href="/wiki/Gavril_B%C4%83nulescu-Bodoni" title="Gavril Bănulescu-Bodoni">
        Gavril Bănulescu-Bodoni
       </a>
       were able to produce books and liturgical works in Moldavian between 1815–1820.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The linguistic situation in Bessarabia from 1812 to 1918 was the gradual development of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingualism" title="Bilingualism">
        bilingualism
       </a>
       . Russian continued to develop as the official language of privilege, whereas Romanian remained the principal vernacular.
      </p>
      <p>
       The period from 1905 to 1917 was one of increasing linguistic conflict, with the re-awakening of Romanian national consciousness. In 1905 and 1906, the Bessarabian
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Zemstvo" title="Zemstvo">
         zemstva
        </a>
       </i>
       asked for the re-introduction of Romanian in schools as a "compulsory language", and the "liberty to teach in the mother language (Romanian language)". At the same time, Romanian-language newspapers and journals began to appear, such as
       <i>
        Basarabia
       </i>
       (1906),
       <i>
        Viața Basarabiei
       </i>
       (1907),
       <i>
        Moldovanul
       </i>
       (1907),
       <i>
        Luminătorul
       </i>
       (1908),
       <i>
        Cuvînt moldovenesc
       </i>
       (1913),
       <i>
        Glasul Basarabiei
       </i>
       (1913). From 1913, the synod permitted that "the churches in
       <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">
        Bessarabia
       </a>
       use the Romanian language". Romanian finally became the official language with the
       <a href="/wiki/1923_Constitution_of_Romania" title="1923 Constitution of Romania">
        Constitution of 1923
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_grammar">
        Historical grammar
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Historical grammar">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Romanian has preserved a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Declension" title="Declension">
        declension
       </a>
       , but whereas Latin had six
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">
        cases
       </a>
       , from a morphological viewpoint, Romanian has only five: the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nominative" title="Nominative">
        nominative
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accusative" title="Accusative">
        accusative
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genitive" title="Genitive">
        genitive
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dative_case" title="Dative case">
        dative
       </a>
       , and marginally the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vocative" title="Vocative">
        vocative
       </a>
       . Romanian nouns also preserve the neuter
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">
        gender
       </a>
       , although instead of functioning as a separate gender with its own forms in adjectives, the Romanian neuter became a mixture of masculine and feminine. The
       <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">
        verb
       </a>
       morphology of Romanian has shown the same move towards a compound
       <a href="/wiki/Perfect_(grammar)" title="Perfect (grammar)">
        perfect
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Future_tense" title="Future tense">
        future tense
       </a>
       as the other Romance languages. Compared with the other
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       , during its evolution, Romanian simplified the original Latin
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_tense" title="Grammatical tense">
        tense
       </a>
       system in extreme ways,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">
          <span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (June 2013)">
           unreliable source?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       in particular the absence of
       <a href="/wiki/Sequence_of_tenses" title="Sequence of tenses">
        sequence of tenses
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         <small>
          not official:
         </small>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         South Africa
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:right;">
         0.007%
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:right;">
         3,000
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:right;">
         44,819,778
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="4" style="background:#f9f9f9; text-align:left;">
         <p>
          <small>
           <sup>
            1
           </sup>
           Many are Moldavian who were deported
           <br/>
           <sup>
            2
           </sup>
           Data only for the districts on the right bank of Dniester (without Transnistria and the city of Tighina). In Moldova, it is sometimes referred to as the "
           <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">
            Moldovan language
           </a>
           "
           <br/>
           <sup>
            3
           </sup>
           In Transnistria, it is officially called "
           <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">
            Moldovan language
           </a>
           " and is written in
           <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet">
            Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet
           </a>
           .
           <br/>
           <sup>
            4
           </sup>
           Officially divided into Vlachs and Romanians
           <br/>
           <sup>
            5
           </sup>
           Most in Northern Bukovina and Southern Bessarabia; according to a
           <i>
            Moldova Noastră
           </i>
           study (based on the latest Ukrainian census).
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
            <a href="#cite_note-54">
             [53]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </small>
         </p>
        </th>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Romanian is spoken mostly in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
        Balkan region
       </a>
       of Southern Europe, although speakers of the language can be found all over the world, mostly due to emigration of Romanian nationals and the return of immigrants to Romania back to their original countries. Romanian speakers account for 0.5% of the world's population,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 4% of the Romance-speaking population of the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Romanian is the single official and national language in Romania and Moldova, although it shares the official status at regional level with other languages in the Moldovan autonomies of
       <a href="/wiki/Gagauzia" title="Gagauzia">
        Gagauzia
       </a>
       and Transnistria. Romanian is also an official language of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Vojvodina" title="Autonomous Province of Vojvodina">
        Autonomous Province of Vojvodina
       </a>
       in Serbia along with five other languages. Romanian minorities are encountered in Serbia (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timok_Valley" title="Timok Valley">
        Timok Valley
       </a>
       ), Ukraine (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chernivtsi_oblast" title="Chernivtsi oblast">
        Chernivtsi
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odessa_oblast" title="Odessa oblast">
        Odessa oblasts
       </a>
       ), and Hungary (
       <a href="/wiki/Gyula,_Hungary" title="Gyula, Hungary">
        Gyula
       </a>
       ). Large immigrant communities are found in Italy, Spain, France, and Portugal.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1995, the largest Romanian-speaking community in the Middle East was found in Israel, where Romanian was spoken by 5% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Romanian is also spoken as a second language by people from Arabic-speaking countries who have studied in Romania. It is estimated that almost half a million Middle Eastern Arabs studied in Romania during the 1980s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Small Romanian-speaking communities are to be found in Kazakhstan and Russia. Romanian is also spoken within communities of Romanian and Moldovan immigrants in the United States, Canada and Australia, although they do not make up a large homogeneous community statewide.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">
        Legal status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Legal status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_Romania">
        In Romania
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: In Romania">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Romania" title="Constitution of Romania">
        Constitution of Romania
       </a>
       of 1991, as revised in 2003, Romanian is the official language of the Republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Romania mandates the use of Romanian in official government publications, public education and legal contracts. Advertisements as well as other public messages must bear a translation of foreign words,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while trade signs and logos shall be written predominantly in Romanian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Romanian Language Institute (
       <i>
        Institutul Limbii Române
       </i>
       ), established by the Ministry of Education of Romania, promotes Romanian and supports people willing to study the language, working together with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Department for Romanians Abroad.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_Moldova">
        In Moldova
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: In Moldova">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">
        Moldovan language
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Romanian is the official language of the Republic of Moldova. The 1991
       <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Moldovan Declaration of Independence">
        Declaration of Independence
       </a>
       names the official language Romanian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Moldova" title="Constitution of Moldova">
        Constitution of Moldova
       </a>
       names the state language of the country
       <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">
        Moldovan
       </a>
       . In December 2013, a decision of the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Moldova" title="Constitutional Court of Moldova">
        Constitutional Court of Moldova
       </a>
       ruled that the Declaration of Independence takes precedence over the Constitution and the state language should be called Romanian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Scholars agree that Moldovan and Romanian are the same language, with the
       <a href="/wiki/-onym" title="-onym">
        glottonym
       </a>
       "Moldovan" used in certain political contexts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has been the sole official language since the adoption of the Law on State Language of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moldavian_SSR" title="Moldavian SSR">
        Moldavian SSR
       </a>
       in 1989.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This law mandates the use of Moldovan in all the political, economical, cultural and social spheres, as well as asserting the existence of a "linguistic Moldo-Romanian identity".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is also used in schools, mass media, education and in the colloquial speech and writing. Outside the political arena the language is most often called "Romanian". In the breakaway territory of Transnistria, it is co-official with
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">
        Ukrainian
       </a>
       and Russian.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/2014_Moldovan_Census" title="2014 Moldovan Census">
        2014 census
       </a>
       , out of the 2,804,801 people living in Moldova, 24% (652,394) stated Romanian as their most common language, whereas 56% stated Moldovan. While in the urban centers speakers are split evenly between the two names (with the capital Chișinău showing a strong preference for the name "Romanian", i.e. 3:2), in the countryside hardly a quarter of Romanian/Moldovan speakers indicated Romanian as their native language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It should be noted that unofficial results of this census first showed a stronger preference for the name Romanian, however the initial reports were later dismissed by the Institute for Statistics, which led to speculations in the media regarding the forgery of the census results.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="In_Vojvodina.2C_Serbia">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_Vojvodina,_Serbia">
        In Vojvodina, Serbia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: In Vojvodina, Serbia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Official_status_of_Romanian_language_in_Vojvodina" title="Official status of Romanian language in Vojvodina">
        Official status of Romanian language in Vojvodina
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vojvodina_romanian_map.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="647" data-file-width="760" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Vojvodina_romanian_map.png/300px-Vojvodina_romanian_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Vojvodina_romanian_map.png/450px-Vojvodina_romanian_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Vojvodina_romanian_map.png/600px-Vojvodina_romanian_map.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vojvodina_romanian_map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Official usage of Romanian language in
         <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">
          Vojvodina
         </a>
         , Serbia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2034" data-file-width="1337" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png/180px-Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png/270px-Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png/360px-Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romanian_and_Vlach_language_in_Serbia.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Romanian language in entire Serbia
         <i>
          (see also
          <a href="/wiki/Romanians_of_Serbia" title="Romanians of Serbia">
           Romanians of Serbia
          </a>
          )
         </i>
         , census 2002
         <table style="width:100%;">
          <tr>
           <td valign="top">
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #DFB5F7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             1–5%
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #D094EE; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             5–10%
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #B366FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             10–15%
            </div>
           </td>
           <td valign="top">
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #903CC4; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             15–25%
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #6B0194; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             25–35%
            </div>
            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #490165; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             over 35%
            </div>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_Serbia" title="Constitution of the Republic of Serbia">
        Constitution of the Republic of Serbia
       </a>
       determines that in the regions of the Republic of Serbia inhabited by national minorities, their own languages and scripts shall be officially used as well, in the manner established by law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Statute of the Autonomous Province of
       <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">
        Vojvodina
       </a>
       determines that, together with the
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">
        Serbian language
       </a>
       and the Cyrillic script, and the Latin script as stipulated by the law, the
       <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">
        Croat
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">
        Slovak
       </a>
       , Romanian and
       <a href="/wiki/Rusyn_language" title="Rusyn language">
        Rusyn languages
       </a>
       and their scripts, as well as languages and scripts of other nationalities, shall simultaneously be officially used in the work of the bodies of the Autonomous Province of Vojvodina, in the manner established by the law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The bodies of the Autonomous Province of Vojvodina are: the Assembly, the Executive Council and the Provincial administrative bodies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Romanian language and script are officially used in eight municipalities:
       <a href="/wiki/Alibunar" title="Alibunar">
        Alibunar
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biserica_Alb%C4%83_(Vojvodina)" title="Biserica Albă (Vojvodina)">
        Biserica Albă
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">
        Serbian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="sr">
        Bela Crkva
       </span>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ziti%C8%99te" title="Zitiște">
        Zitiște
       </a>
       (Žitište),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zrenianin" title="Zrenianin">
        Zrenianin
       </a>
       (Zrenjanin),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kov%C4%83ci%C8%9Ba" title="Kovăcița">
        Kovăcița
       </a>
       (Kovačica),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuvin" title="Cuvin">
        Cuvin
       </a>
       (Kovin),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plandi%C8%99te" title="Plandiște">
        Plandiște
       </a>
       (Plandište) and
       <a href="/wiki/Se%C4%8Danj" title="Sečanj">
        Sečanj
       </a>
       . In the municipality of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V%C3%A2r%C8%99e%C8%9B" title="Vârșeț">
        Vârșeț
       </a>
       (Vršac), Romanian is official only in the villages of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voivodin%C8%9B" title="Voivodinț">
        Voivodinț
       </a>
       (Vojvodinci),
       <a href="/wiki/Markovac_(Vr%C5%A1ac)" title="Markovac (Vršac)">
        Marcovăț
       </a>
       (Markovac),
       <a href="/wiki/Straja" title="Straja">
        Straja
       </a>
       (Straža),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamu_Mic" title="Jamu Mic">
        Jamu Mic
       </a>
       (Mali Žam),
       <a href="/wiki/Malo_Sredi%C5%A1te" title="Malo Središte">
        Srediștea Mică
       </a>
       (Malo Središte),
       <a href="/wiki/Mesi%C4%87_(Vr%C5%A1ac)" title="Mesić (Vršac)">
        Mesici
       </a>
       (Mesić),
       <a href="/wiki/Jablanka" title="Jablanka">
        Jablanka
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sal%C4%8Dica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Salčica (page does not exist)">
        Sălcița
       </a>
       (Salčica),
       <a href="/wiki/Riti%C5%A1evo" title="Ritiševo">
        Râtișor
       </a>
       (Ritiševo),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ore%C8%99a%C8%9B" title="Oreșaț">
        Oreșaț
       </a>
       (Orašac) and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Co%C8%99tei&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Coștei (page does not exist)">
        Coștei
       </a>
       (Kuštilj).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 2002 Census, the last carried out in Serbia, 1.5% of Vojvodinians stated Romanian as their native language.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_language_status_in_Ukraine">
        Regional language status in Ukraine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Regional language status in Ukraine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In parts of Ukraine where
       <a href="/wiki/Romanians_in_Ukraine" title="Romanians in Ukraine">
        Romanians
       </a>
       constitute a significant share of the local population (districts in
       <a href="/wiki/Chernivtsi_Oblast" title="Chernivtsi Oblast">
        Chernivtsi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Odessa_Oblast" title="Odessa Oblast">
        Odessa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zakarpattia_Oblast" title="Zakarpattia Oblast">
        Zakarpattia
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">
        oblasts
       </a>
       ) Romanian is taught in schools as a primary language and there are Romanian-language newspapers, TV, and radio broadcasting.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Chernivtsi" title="University of Chernivtsi">
        University of Chernivtsi
       </a>
       in western Ukraine trains teachers for Romanian schools in the fields of Romanian philology, mathematics and physics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Hertsa_Raion" title="Hertsa Raion">
        Hertsa Raion
       </a>
       of Ukraine as well as in other villages of
       <a href="/wiki/Chernivtsi_Oblast" title="Chernivtsi Oblast">
        Chernivtsi Oblast
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zakarpattia_Oblast" title="Zakarpattia Oblast">
        Zakarpattia Oblast
       </a>
       , Romanian has been declared a "regional language" alongside Ukrainian as per the 2012
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislation_on_languages_in_Ukraine" title="Legislation on languages in Ukraine">
        legislation on languages in Ukraine
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_other_countries_and_organizations">
        In other countries and organizations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: In other countries and organizations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Romanian_diaspora" title="Romanian diaspora">
        Romanian diaspora
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Romanian is an official or administrative language in various communities and organisations, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">
        Latin Union
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       . Romanian is also one of the five languages in which religious services are performed in the autonomous monastic state of
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Athos" title="Mount Athos">
        Mount Athos
       </a>
       , spoken in the monk communities of
       <a href="/wiki/Prodromos_(Mount_Athos)" title="Prodromos (Mount Athos)">
        Prodromos
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lacu_(Mount_Athos)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lacu (Mount Athos) (page does not exist)">
        Lacu
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diagram%C4%83LimbaRom%C3%A2n%C4%83.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="341" data-file-width="699" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Diagram%C4%83LimbaRom%C3%A2n%C4%83.png/350px-Diagram%C4%83LimbaRom%C3%A2n%C4%83.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Diagram%C4%83LimbaRom%C3%A2n%C4%83.png/525px-Diagram%C4%83LimbaRom%C3%A2n%C4%83.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Diagram%C4%83LimbaRom%C3%A2n%C4%83.png 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diagram%C4%83LimbaRom%C3%A2n%C4%83.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Distribution of first-language native Romanian speakers by country—
         <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">
          Voivodina
         </a>
         is an autonomous province of northern
         <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
          Serbia
         </a>
         bordering Romania, while
         <i>
          Altele
         </i>
         means "Other"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_second_and_foreign_language">
        As a second and foreign language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: As a second and foreign language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Romanian is taught in some areas that have Romanian minority communities, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">
        Vojvodina
       </a>
       in Serbia, Bulgaria, Ukraine and Hungary. The
       <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Cultural_Institute" title="Romanian Cultural Institute">
        Romanian Cultural Institute
       </a>
       (ICR) has since 1992 organised summer courses in Romanian for language teachers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also non-Romanians who study Romanian as a foreign language, for example the Nicolae Bălcescu High-school in
       <a href="/wiki/Gyula,_Hungary" title="Gyula, Hungary">
        Gyula
       </a>
       , Hungary.
      </p>
      <p>
       Romanian is taught as a
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_language" title="Foreign language">
        foreign language
       </a>
       in tertiary institutions, mostly in European countries such as Germany, France and Italy, and the Netherlands, as well as in the United States. Overall, it is taught as a foreign language in 43 countries around the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Knowledge_Romanian_Eastern_EU.png">

        </a>
