          <tr>
           <td colspan="31" style="background:#efefef; text-align:center;">
            <b>
             Phonemes
            </b>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr style="text-align:center;">
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /a/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ə/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ɨ/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /b/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /k/,
             <br/>
             /t͡ʃ/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /d/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /e/,
             <br/>
             /e̯/,
             <br/>
             /je/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /f/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ɡ/,
             <br/>
             /d͡ʒ/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /h/,
             <br/>
             mute
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /i/,
             <br/>
             /j/,
             <br/>
             /ʲ/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ɨ/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ʒ/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /k/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /l/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /m/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /n/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /o/,
             <br/>
             /o̯/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /p/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /k/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /r/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /s/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ʃ/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /t/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /t͡s/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /u/,
             <br/>
             /w/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /v/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /v/,
             <br/>
             /w/,
             <br/>
             /u/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ks/,
             <br/>
             /ɡz/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /j/,
             <br/>
             /i/
            </span>
           </td>
           <td>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /z/
            </span>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </dd>
       </dl>
      </center>
      <p>
       K, Q, W and Y, not part of the native alphabet, were officially introduced in the Romanian alphabet in 1982 and are mostly used to write loanwords like
       <i>
        kilogram
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        quasar
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        watt
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        yoga
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Romanian alphabet is based on the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">
        Latin script
       </a>
       with five additional letters
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <a href="/wiki/%C4%82" title="Ă">
          Ă
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <a href="/wiki/%C3%82" title="Â">
          Â
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <a href="/wiki/%C3%8E" title="Î">
          Î
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C8%98" title="Ș">
          Ș
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="ro">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C8%9A" title="Ț">
          Ț
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       . Formerly, there were as many as 12 additional letters, but some of them were abolished in subsequent reforms. Also, until the early 20th century, a short vowel marker was used.
      </p>
      <p>
       Today the Romanian alphabet is largely
       <a href="/wiki/Phonemic_orthography" title="Phonemic orthography">
        phonemic
       </a>
       . However, the letters
       <i>
        â
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        î
       </i>
       both represent the same
       <a href="/wiki/Close_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Close central unrounded vowel">
        close central unrounded vowel
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɨ/
       </span>
       .
       <i>
        Â
       </i>
       is used only inside words;
       <i>
        î
       </i>
       is used at the beginning or the end of non-compound words and in the middle of compound words. Another exception from a completely phonetic writing system is the fact that
       <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">
        vowels
       </a>
       and their respective
       <a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">
        semivowels
       </a>
       are not distinguished in writing. In dictionaries the distinction is marked by separating the entry word into
       <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">
        syllables
       </a>
       for words containing a
       <a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(linguistics)" title="Hiatus (linguistics)">
        hiatus
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Stressed vowels also are not marked in writing, except very rarely in cases where by misplacing the stress a word might change its meaning and if the meaning is not obvious from the context. For example,
       <i>
        trei copíi
       </i>
       means "three children" while
       <i>
        trei cópii
       </i>
       means "three copies".
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">
        Pronunciation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Pronunciation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1028" data-file-width="1844" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg/200px-Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg/300px-Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg/400px-Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romanian_keyboard_letters.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A close shot of some keys with Romanian characters on the keyboard of a laptop
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Romanian_alphabet#Î_versus_Â" title="Romanian alphabet">
        Romanian alphabet § Î versus Â
       </a>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         h
        </i>
        is not silent like in other Romance languages such as Spanish, Italian, Portuguese, Catalan and French, but represents the phoneme
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /h/
        </span>
        , except in the digraphs
        <i>
         ch
        </i>
        /k/ and
        <i>
         gh
        </i>
        /g/ (see below)
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         j
        </i>
        represents
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʒ/
        </span>
        , as in French, Catalan or Portuguese (the sound spelled with
        <i>
         s
        </i>
        in the English words "vision, pleasure, treasure").
       </li>
       <li>
        There are two letters with a comma below,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C8%98" title="Ș">
         Ș
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C8%9A" title="Ț">
         Ț
        </a>
        , which represent the sounds
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʃ/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /t͡s/
        </span>
        . However, the allographs with a cedilla instead of a comma,
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/%C5%9E" title="Ş">
          Ş
         </a>
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%A2" title="Ţ">
          Ţ
         </a>
        </i>
        , became widespread when pre-
        <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">
         Unicode
        </a>
        and early Unicode
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Character_sets" title="Character sets">
         character sets
        </a>
        did not include the standard form.
       </li>
       <li>
        A final orthographical
        <i>
         i
        </i>
        after a consonant often represents the palatalization of the consonant (e.g.,
        <i>
         lup
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /lup/
        </span>
        "wolf" vs.
        <i>
         lupi
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /lupʲ/
        </span>
        "wolves") – it is
        <i>
         not
        </i>
        pronounced like Italian
        <i>
         lupi
        </i>
        (which also means "wolves"), and is an example of the
        <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">
         Slavic
        </a>
        influence on Romanian.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         ă
        </i>
        represents the
        <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">
         schwa
        </a>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ə/
        </span>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         î
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         â
        </i>
        both represent the sound
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɨ/
        </span>
        . In rapid speech (for example in the name of the country) the
        <i>
         â
        </i>
        sound may sound similar to a casual listener to the short
        <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">
         schwa
        </a>
        sound
        <i>
         ă
        </i>
        (in fact,
        <a href="/wiki/Aromanian_language" title="Aromanian language">
         Aromanian
        </a>
        does merge the two, writing them
        <i>
         ã
        </i>
        ) but careful speakers will distinguish the sound. The nearest equivalent is the vowel in the last syllable of the word
        <i>
         roses
        </i>
        for some English speakers. It is also roughly equivalent to European Portuguese
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɐ/
        </span>
        , the Polish
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        or the Russian
        <i>
         ы
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The letter
        <i>
         e
        </i>
        generally represents the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid_front" title="Mid front">
         mid front unrounded
        </a>
        vowel
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [e]
        </span>
        , somewhat like in the English word
        <i>
         s
         <b>
          e
         </b>
         t
        </i>
        . However, the letter
        <i>
         e
        </i>
        is pronounced as
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [je]
        </span>
        ([j] sounds like 'y' in 'you') when it is the first letter of any form of the verb
        <i>
         a fi
        </i>
        "to be", or of a personal pronoun, for instance
        <i>
         este
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /jeste/
        </span>
        "is" and
        <i>
         el
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /jel/
        </span>
        "he".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
         <a href="#cite_note-105">
          [104]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
         <a href="#cite_note-106">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
        This addition of the semivowel
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /j/
        </span>
        does not occur in more recent loans and their derivatives, such as
        <i>
         eră
        </i>
        "era",
        <i>
         electric
        </i>
        "electric" etc. Some words (such as
        <i>
         iepure
        </i>
        "hare", formerly spelled
        <i>
         epure
        </i>
        ) are now written with the initial
        <i>
         i
        </i>
        to indicate the semivowel.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        represents either the phoneme sequence
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ks/
        </span>
        as in
        <i>
         expresie
        </i>
        = expression, or
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡz/
        </span>
        as in
        <i>
         exemplu
        </i>
        = example, as in English.
       </li>
       <li>
        As in Italian, the letters
        <i>
         c
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         g
        </i>
        represent the affricates
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /tʃ/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dʒ/
        </span>
        before
        <i>
         i
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         e
        </i>
        , and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /k/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡ/
        </span>
        elsewhere. When
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /k/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡ/
        </span>
        are followed by vowels
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /e/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /i/
        </span>
        (or their corresponding
        <a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">
         semivowels
        </a>
        or the final
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʲ/
        </span>
        ) the digraphs
        <i>
         ch
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         gh
        </i>
        are used instead of
        <i>
         c
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         g
        </i>
        , as shown in the table below. Unlike Italian, however, Romanian uses
        <i>
         ce-
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         ge-
        </i>
        to write
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /t͡ʃ/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /d͡ʒ/
        </span>
        before a back vowel instead of
        <i>
         ci-
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         gi-
        </i>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Group
        </th>
        <th>
         Phoneme
        </th>
        <th>
         Pronunciation
        </th>
        <th>
         Examples
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         ce, ci
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /tʃ/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          ch
         </i>
         in
         <b>
          chest
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          cheek
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          cerc
         </i>
         (circle),
         <i>
          ceașcă
         </i>
         (cup),
         <i>
          cercel
         </i>
         (earring),
         <i>
          cină
         </i>
         (dinner),
         <i>
          ciocan
         </i>
         (hammer)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         che, chi
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /k/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          k
         </i>
         in
         <b>
          kettle
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          kiss
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          cheie
         </i>
         (key),
         <i>
          chelner
         </i>
         (waiter),
         <i>
          chioșc
         </i>
         (kiosk),
         <i>
          chitară
         </i>
         (guitar),
         <i>
          ureche
         </i>
         (ear)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         ge, gi
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /dʒ/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          j
         </i>
         in
         <b>
          jelly
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          jigsaw
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          ger
         </i>
         (frost),
         <i>
          gimnast
         </i>
         (gymnast),
         <i>
          gem
         </i>
         (jam),
         <i>
          girafă
         </i>
         (giraffe),
         <i>
          geantă
         </i>
         (bag)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         ghe, ghi
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ɡ/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          g
         </i>
         in
         <b>
          get
         </b>
         ,
         <b>
          give
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          ghețar
         </i>
         (glacier),
         <i>
          ghid
         </i>
         (guide),
         <i>
          ghindă
         </i>
         (acorn),
         <i>
          ghidon
         </i>
         (handle bar),
         <i>
          stingher
         </i>
         (lonely)
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation_and_capitalization">
        Punctuation and capitalization
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Punctuation and capitalization">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Uses of punctuation peculiar to Romanian are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The quotation marks use the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quotation_mark,_non-English_usage#Polish" title="Quotation mark, non-English usage">
         Polish format
        </a>
        in the format "quote "inside" quote", that is, ". . ." for a normal quotation, and double angle symbols for a quotation inside a quotation.
       </li>
       <li>
        Proper quotations which span multiple paragraphs do not start each paragraph with the quotation marks; one single pair of quotation marks is always used, regardless of how many paragraphs are quoted.
       </li>
       <li>
        Dialogues are identified with
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quotation_mark,_non-English_usage#Quotation_dash" title="Quotation mark, non-English usage">
         quotation dashes
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Serial_comma" title="Serial comma">
         Oxford comma
        </a>
        before "and" is considered incorrect ("red, yellow and blue" is the proper format).
       </li>
       <li>
        Punctuation signs which follow a text in parentheses always follow the final bracket.
       </li>
       <li>
        In titles, only the first letter of the first word is capitalized, the rest of the title using sentence capitalization (with all its rules: proper names are capitalized as usual, etc.).
       </li>
       <li>
        Names of months and days are not capitalized (
        <i>
         ianuarie
        </i>
        "January",
        <i>
         joi
        </i>
        "Thursday").
       </li>
       <li>
        Adjectives derived from proper names are not capitalized (
        <i>
         Germania
        </i>
        "Germany", but
        <i>
         german
        </i>
        "German").
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spelling_issues_between_Romania_and_Moldova">
        Spelling issues between Romania and Moldova
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Spelling issues between Romania and Moldova">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Prior to 2010, there existed a minor spelling difference between standard forms of Romanian language used in Romania and the variant (also called
       <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">
        Moldovan
       </a>
       ) used in the Republic of Moldova—the
       <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_of_Moldova" title="Academy of Sciences of Moldova">
        Academy of Sciences of Moldova
       </a>
       did not switch to the new spelling rules introduced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Academy" title="Romanian Academy">
        Romanian Academy
       </a>
       in 1993. In 2000, the Moldovan Academy recommended adopting the spelling rules used in Romania,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in 2010 the Academy launched a schedule for the transition to the new rules that was completed in 2011 (regarding publications) and is currently under implementation in the educational system (due to be completed within two school years). However, as of 2015 most Moldovan commercial websites maintain the 'old' spelling.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood.
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <i>
           (
           <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">
            Universal Declaration of Human Rights
           </a>
           )
          </i>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Romanian – highlighted words were
       <i>
        directly
       </i>
       derived from Latin:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         Toate
        </b>
        <b>
         ființele
        </b>
        umane
        <b>
         se
        </b>
        <b>
         nasc
        </b>
        libere
        <b>
         și
        </b>
        egale
        <b>
         în
        </b>
        demnitate
        <b>
         și
        </b>
        <b>
         în
        </b>
        <b>
         drepturi
        </b>
        .
        <b>
         Ele
        </b>
        <b>
         sunt
        </b>
        <b>
         înzestrate
        </b>
        <b>
         cu
        </b>
        rațiune
        <b>
         și
        </b>
        conștiință
        <b>
         și
        </b>
        trebuie
        <b>
         să
        </b>
        <b>
         se
        </b>
        comporte
        <b>
         unele
        </b>
        <b>
         față
        </b>
        <b>
         de
        </b>
        <b>
         altele
        </b>
        <b>
         în
        </b>
        spiritul fraternității.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Contemporary Romanian – highlighted words are French or Italian
       <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">
        loanwords
       </a>
       :
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Toate ființele
        <b>
         umane
        </b>
        se nasc
        <b>
         libere
        </b>
        și
        <b>
         egale
        </b>
        în
        <b>
         demnitate
        </b>
        și în drepturi. Ele sunt înzestrate cu
        <b>
         rațiune
        </b>
        și
        <b>
         conștiință
        </b>
        și trebuie să se
        <b>
         comporte
        </b>
        unele față de altele în
        <b>
         spiritul
        </b>
        <b>
         fraternității
        </b>
        .
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Romanian, excluding French and Italian loanwords – highlighted words are Slavic loanwords:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Toate ființele omenești se nasc
        <b>
         slobode
        </b>
        și
        <b>
         deopotrivă
        </b>
        în
        <b>
         destoinicie
        </b>
        și în drepturi. Ele sunt înzestrate cu înțelegere și cuget și
        <b>
         trebuie
        </b>
        să se poarte unele față de altele în
        <b>
         duh
        </b>
        de frățietate.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Romanian, excluding loanwords and having almost the same meaning:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Toate ființele omenești se nasc nesupuse și asemenea în prețuire și în drepturi. Ele sunt înzestrate cu înțelegere și cuget și se cuvine să se poarte unele față de altele după firea frăției.
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="mw-references-wrap">
       <ol class="references">
        <li id="cite_note-Moldova-9">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-Moldova_9-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          The constitution of the Republic of Moldova refers to the country's language as
          <i>
           Moldovan
          </i>
          , whilst the 1991
          <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Moldovan Declaration of Independence">
           Declaration of Independence
          </a>
          names the official language
          <i>
           Romanian
          </i>
          . In December 2013, a decision of the
          <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Moldova" title="Constitutional Court of Moldova">
           Constitutional Court of Moldova
          </a>
          ruled that the Declaration of Independence takes precedence over the Constitution and that the state language is therefore Romanian, not "Moldovan".
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2013/12/05/moldovan-court-rules-official-language-is-romanian-replacing-soviet-flavored/" rel="nofollow">
           "Moldovan court rules official language is 'Romanian,' replacing Soviet-flavored 'Moldovan'"
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
      </div>

         <span class="reference-text">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.iatp.md/ladom/downloads/M3.doc" rel="nofollow">
           Legea cu privire la functionarea limbilor vorbite pe teritoriul RSS Moldovenesti Nr.3465-XI din 01.09.89 Vestile nr.9/217, 1989
          </a>

          <i>
           "Moldavian RSS supports the desire of the Moldavian that live across the borders of the Republic, and – considering the existing Moldo-Romanian linguistic identity – of the Romanians that live on the territory of the USSR, of doing their studies and satisfying their cultural needs in their maternal language."

          <span class="languageicon">
           (in Romanian)
          </span>

          <i>
           e
          </i>
          in some personal pronouns:
          <a class="external text" href="http://dexonline.ro/search.php?cuv=el" rel="nofollow">

           </i>
           ,
           <i>
            ei
           </i>
           , etc.
          </a>

          <i>
           a fi
          </i>
          (
          <i>
           to be
          </i>
          ):

               </a>
               .

                    Italics
                   </i>
                   indicate
                   <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">
                    extinct languages
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   <b>
                    Bold
                   </b>
                   indicates
                   <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">
                    languages with more than 5 million speakers
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   Languages between parentheses are
                   <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">
                    varieties
                   </a>
                   of the language on their left.
